Multiple Definitions of Fitra
Author presents ten numbered definitions of fitra from various sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse and categorize the various definitions of fitra presented in this passage.

Core Idea
Fitra is defined across theological, epistemological, and psychological domains.

This passage presents ten numbered definitions of fitra from different sources, including philosophical, theological, and psychological perspectives. Your task is to identify the key elements of each definition and understand how they relate to one another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of each definition
Note that some definitions are attributed (e.g., Imam al-Baqir) and some are from the author. This helps understand the authority behind each definition.
Definition 17 is attributed to Imam al-Baqir.
2
Extract the genus and differentia for each definition
For each definition, identify what fitra is said to be (genus) and what distinguishes it (differentia). For example, definition 10 says fitra is 'practical intellect' (genus) used for bodily and spiritual benefit (differentia).
3
Classify each definition by domain
Determine whether the definition is theological (relating to God), epistemological (relating to knowledge), or psychological (relating to drives and instincts). For instance, definition 14 is theological, definition 12 is epistemological, definition 18 is psychological.
4
Compare the definitions for consistency and conflict
Do any definitions contradict each other? How do they overlap? Definition 10 (practical intellect) and definition 18 (drives) seem to cover different aspects, so they may be complementary rather than conflicting.
5
Synthesize the common core
What is the common thread among all definitions? All definitions treat fitra as something innate, original, and constitutive of human nature. The author's synthetic definition at the end attempts to unify them.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۰ - هي ( العقل العملي (١) كما هو ملاحظ في استعمال الجوارح والقوى في مصلحة بدن الانسان وعقل فيما يعود على النفس كمالاً ۱۱ - ( إنها الشيء الذي لا يتبدل في الروح والجسد)٢ ١٢- (هي الخلقة والهيئة التي في نفس الطفل والتي هي معدة، ومهيأة لأن يميز بها مصنوعات الله ، ويستدل بها على ربه، ويعرف شرائعه ويؤمن به ۳ ۱۳ (هي) تلك الحالة الواعية الاصيلة في شخصية الإنسان التي من خلالها يهتدي إلى الاشياء وتنطوي على مجموعة من الميول والمعارف ركبت وركزت في أعماق الإنسان و تعد من لوازم وجوده) ١٤- هي من الألطاف التي خص الله تعالى بها الإنسان من بين جميع المخلوقات ، إذ إن الموجودات الأخرى غير الإنسان إما أنها لا تملك مثل هذه الفطرة المذكورة ، وإما أن لها حظاً ضئيلاً منها ۱۷ - الامام محمد بن علي الباقر - ع - فسر الفطرة بانها المعرفة ٦ أي معرفة جميع مباديء الخلقة ان الفطرة موضوع يبتعد عن التعريف والقولبة ويقترب من الفهم والادراك وبالتالي يمكننا القول : ان الفطرة هي القانون العام الذي يسري على عالم الاشياء ولا يتبدل . أو : هي الهيئة الخاصة التي خلق بها الإنسان وفيها تلك الخصائص التي أودعها الله فيه وميزه عن بقية خلقه ولو استخدمنا مصطلحات علم النفس نقول: ۱۸ - الفطرة هي مجموع الدوافع والضوابط النفسية والجسدية والهرمونية التي تنظم حياة الفرد وبعبارة اشمل : هي مجموع الهرمونات المادية في الجسم (الغرائز) والهرمونات النفسية (الطبائع) موضوعة في قالب مشترك عام اسمه الفطرة
10. It is (practical intellect (1) as observed in the use of limbs and faculties for the benefit of the body, and intellect regarding what returns to the soul as perfection. 11. (It is the thing that does not change in spirit and body) (2). 12. (It is the creation and disposition which is in the child's soul, which is prepared and readied for him to distinguish by it God's creations, and to deduce by it his Lord, and to know His laws and believe in Him) (3). 13. (It is) that original conscious state in the personality of man through which he is guided to things, and it includes a set of inclinations and knowledge that are installed and fixed in the depths of man, and it is among the necessities of his existence. 14. It is among the favors with which God Almighty distinguished man among all creatures, for other existents besides man either do not possess such mentioned fitra, or have a small share of it. 17. Imam Muhammad ibn Ali al-Baqir (peace be upon him) interpreted fitra as knowledge (6), i.e., knowledge of all principles of creation. Fitra is a subject that stays away from definition and formulation and approaches understanding and perception. Therefore, we can say: Fitra is the general law that applies to the world of things and does not change. Or: It is the special disposition with which man was created, and in it are those characteristics that God placed in him and distinguished him from the rest of His creation. If we use psychological terms, we say: 18. Fitra is the totality of psychological, physical, and hormonal drives and controls that organize the individual's life. In a more comprehensive phrase: It is the totality of material hormones in the body (instincts) and psychological hormones (dispositions) placed in a common general mold called fitra.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents a series of definitions of fitra from various Islamic scholars. The author begins by citing definitions from other works, each numbered. Definition 10 identifies fitra with practical intellect, both in bodily actions and spiritual perfection. Definition 11 emphasizes its unchanging nature. Definition 12 (from al-Khazraji?) describes it as the innate disposition in children to recognize God's creation and deduce His existence. Definition 13 calls it an original conscious state comprising inclinations and knowledge. Definition 14 views it as a divine favor exclusive to humans. Then Imam al-Baqir's definition identifies fitra with knowledge of all principles of creation. The author then offers his own synthetic definition: fitra is the general immutable law governing things, or the special disposition containing God-given characteristics. Finally, definition 18 from a psychological perspective describes fitra as the sum of psychophysical and hormonal drives. The variety shows that fitra is understood on multiple levels: theological, epistemological, and psychological.

Key Terms
الفطرة
العقل العملي
الغرائز
الطبائع

Key Takeaway
Fitra is a multifaceted concept that spans theological, epistemological, and psychological domains, and no single definition captures its full meaning.
